<rating>5</rating>< Text>
All I can say is RIBS!!

This place has great ribs.  If you like super tender ribs, this place is for you.  The sauce is a bit tangy and sweet, which must be the Kansas City style of sauce, if so, call me a fan of KC BBQ.

Although everything else on the menu is decent, I wouldn't say it stands out as much as the ribs.  I tend to prefer the long-end ribs.  They are meatier and fattier..hehe... The times I've been here, the brisket has been either hit or miss.  The beef links were good.  You get a lot of bread to slop up the excess sauce on your plate, which is a great thing because when you have so much meat, the added starch is a welcome break.  Sides were good too.

One note of caution is that if you're not a fan of tang in your food, this might not be the best place for you<//Text>

< text>
The choice for me was chicken and links. Just ok but edible. A little on the dry side. The sauce tasty but I had better. Beans just ok and potato salad need more help.

What I was taken in on were the historical pictures of African Americans from years past that decorated the walls. For me it told a story of our past here in America and how we survived those most horrible conditions and were able to come out on the other side battered, bruised but still with our dignity.

I will give them another shot at the dinner plate but will always return to receive more of that precious history that gives us the strength to move forward with our heads up.<//text>

<response>None< /response>< review>
Love renting from this location because Richard is the BEST.  Okay that's not to say that the other employees aren't great as well, but Richard is the man!

What's not to love about a rental car location where you can pull up and be at the front counter within 1 minute with no waiting. Unless you're unlucky and someone happens to be ahead of you.  But usually there's no one in line.

Great selection of cars, most are one-way drop offs from other locations and states.

I've rented here more than 30 times and always get upgraded from the cheapest economy car to either full size, SUV, or sports car, depending on what they have available.

Very rarely are economy cars in stock so keep that in mind because if you absolutely do not want an upgrade because of the possible extra gas cost, then this might not be the rental location for you.

There are 3 gas stations within a couple of miles so you can wait until you get close to fill up (Chevron - right off the freeway, Shell - 1 block east of the airport, and another Shell - about 3 blocks east of the airport).</review>

<UserId.>100606517251204473426<//UserId.>< Name>
J Tran< /Name>
< time>
1616106282532< /time>
<rate>5</rate>< Review>
Definitely up there as far as poke places (although I've only been to 6 different poke places across NorCal).

Base: daikon salad was really interesting, almost like seaweed noodles except the texture was less crunchy and definitely more flavorful. They also added a bit of seasoning I think, which was really nice.

Fish: spicy salmon: not really spicy and the marinade wasn't very flavorful but otherwise had above-average freshness.

Toppings: they are generous with the toppings, I can't believe masago doesn't cost extra! The size that the cucumbers were cut into offered a much better mouth feel than other places. No comment on the other toppings.

Sauces: ohhhh boy the garlic miso was solid, not too sweet not too salty. I could eat it by the spoonful.

House shoyu was good too, I'm not knowledgeable enough about shoyu to have a good comment though.

Overall this meal was fantastic and only $15 including tax for 4 scoops it's a relatively good deal. The highlight of this bowl was that it wasn't overly sweet like other poke places (a lot of poke places go to the more creamy/sweet side of things due to the standard American palate).<//Review>

<userid>111069132501077801670<//userid><name>Rama Duvvuri< /name><Time>1609511429834<//Time><rate>5< /rate>< Review>
We stopped here while we were driving through the area.   I've had Avatar's Punjabi burrito before and thought it was ok, but not as good as Curry Up Now.   I found the enchiladas we ordered at this location quite excellent and look forward to coming back.

We had the smoked eggplant and mixed vegetables, both of which were good and had different sauces and thus pretty different tastes (and it isn't weird to order both for the same table). They are smothered in sauce so it isn't the easiest to eat as takeout.

We also ordered the mushrooms appetizer and some fries (for the kid) and neither of these dishes were things I would want to order again.  The fries were too soft and the mushrooms far too oily.< /Review>

<user_id>106689967933838920220</user_id><name>Srikumar Chari<//name><date>1567488675142</date>< Rate>

< review>
Nice Indian restaurant with a twist. We went after it was mentioned in the Check please (KQED) program. The offer a couple traditional Indian appetizers, like Samosa. The entrees have both a Mexican twist, i.e., chicken enchiladas but the spicing is all Indian. The Italian style entrees are Indian entrees served on a bed of zucchini spaghetti, etc. But the kicker is actually different, the chef/owner of the place asks if he can bring entrees of his choice. Three vegetarians on the table went with that option - they were quite happy with the selection. I went with the chicken enchiladas, very good interesting flavors - Indian, plus traditional Mexican flavors and the side rice is Indian style. The owner makes a fun game out of the chef's choice entrees - he asks you to guess what the vegetables are, if you get all of them right the entire meal is free! I don't know if anyone got all right, we gave up about 30% of the way.

The place is a bit small, so cozy is the word. It can get crowded. Note in Google maps directions - it asks you to take that last right and claims.you've arrived... Not really you have to turn into the strip and the 3rd place is Avatar's.

Bottom line, worth a visit.</review>

<text>Everything we ordered was absolutely delicious. From the vegetable samosas to the chicken curry to the mango lassi, not one item was a disappointment. The vegetable samosas were perfectly crispy and flavorful and the sauce was a great tangy/spicy complement. The white meat chicken was juicy and absorbed the curry. The mango lassi was so unique and incredibly tasty.
Lastly, we chose to get the one dessert Avatar offers, which is a slice of gelato cake with a biscuit crust garnished with whole pistachios. I am so glad I opted for the dessert because it's actually one of the best desserts I've ever had. The total came out to about $36 for two people.

Not a single complaint for Avatar's. Probably one of the best restaurants and the price ($$) was very reasonable. < Text>
5 of us went there over the labor day weekend. Overall I'd say the food is good but not great. The concept is interesting... it's basically Indian fused with classic Mexican and Italian dishes. The owner certainly tries his best to provide a memorable experience, but he came across as a bit overwhelming at times and perhaps oversold his ideas.

If you're looking for great Indian food, there are a number of other places in the bay area that are beyond amazing. As a novelty experience this is worth a try.< /Text>

I made a reservation in advance before arriving. Encountered a small place with very limited seating. I was seated at the counter right in front of the kitchen and stove where all the meals were prepared. This was very interesting to me since I was able to see food cooked and plated, and the extraordinary amount of coordination this operation takes. I was disappointed by how eagerly patrons were admitted into the restaurant even when there seemed to be no space, not to already mention how it seemed there were not enough staff to handle the patrons they were already feverishly serving. It was something to experience once but I will not be back unless they either acquire a larger venue or develop a process to better handle the flow of seating and serving of patrons.< /review>

<name>Neha Kapoor</name><Gmap_id>0x808585050d11d18d:0xe1d770086a096be< /Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

<pictures>None< /pictures><Rate>5<//Rate><time>1532978681858</time>< Review>
This review focuses on the vegetarian dishes we had at Avatar's. Imagine being able to order flavorful dishes made from ingredients used in traditional Indian cooking, an alien concept in a vast majority of Indian restaurants in the US. I personally don't have a problem with the Indian restaurant experience, but after a while, it starts to get repetitive - it's the same set of dishes on the menu everywhere (at least this seems to be the case for the vegetarian section of the menu). The guys at Avatar's excel at using not-so-commonly used veggies and greens in their preparations. Then, they take it up a notch and make fusion dishes out of these ingredients, which is simply mind blowing. The entire experience of the visit was awesome, not very different from some of the other reviewers here. Definitely going back.
An afterthought: We had been a little skeptical about going to the place after an underwhelming experience at one of the other branches of Avatar's in the area months ago. But the amount of positive feedback we got about the place, especially even from non-Indians, made the itch to pay a visit at least once irresistible. This is a completely different and unique experience.</Review>

<UserId.>112963650635319312928< /UserId.><name>Keshav Saharia<//name><Time>1536529803490<//Time>< rate>
5</rate>
< Text>
This is by far the best Indian restaurant in the Bay Area. I make this bold statement as an Indian person with a talented cook for a mother and countless experiences eating at Indian restaurants while growing up in the area. This restaurant best exemplifies healthy, tasteful Indian cuisine, as well as some incredible fusion dishes (I had to go back several times to try all the Punjabi enchiladas). The masala chai is always freshly made to order, and you can be confident that anything you order is made with the best ingredients.

By food quality alone this place deserves 5 stars. The owner, a delightful man who greets every customer and takes every order, will make your experience personalized and extraordinary. Aside from his deep knowledge as a nutritionist, he is deeply engaged in the customer experience and is a perfect example of how to run a successful business for decades. Just as his food exemplifies healthy and tasteful food of India, his personality exemplifies the work ethic and dharmic sense of responsibility of India.

This is truly one of the hidden gems of California and I whole-heartedly recommend this restaurant to everyone.</Text>
